# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

59-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive analysis of Prometheus metric registration patterns across the three repositories and created `/workspace/answer.json` with the findings.

## Summary

I've documented how Prometheus metrics are registered and exposed in each repository:

### **Kubernetes**: Centralized Registry with Lazy Registration
- Uses `k8s.io/component-base/metrics` package for metric creation
- Registers via `legacyregistry.MustRegister()` in a `sync.Once` pattern
- Lazy initialization through explicit `Register()` functions
- Includes stability levels (ALPHA, STABLE) for metrics

### **Prometheus**: Dual Pattern (Flexible)
- **Auto-registration**: Uses `promauto.NewCounter/Histogram/Gauge` in storage/remote
- **Manual registration**: Uses `prometheus.New*` constructors with `r.MustRegister()` in notifier and scrape subsystems
- Supports both global and custom registries

### **Grafana**: Global Auto-Registration
- Exclusively uses `promauto.NewCounter/Histogram/GaugeVec` 
- Metrics declared at package level in var blocks
- Automatic registration at module load time
- No explicit registration calls needed

The answer includes 20 specific source files, 9 key symbols demonstrating registration, call chains showing how registration flows work, and a detailed narrative comparing the three approaches.

Registration occurs through `legacyregistry.MustRegister()` (staging/src/k8s.io/component-base/metrics/legacyregistry/registry.go:37), typically within a `sync.Once` pattern to ensure single registration. The `Register()` function (pkg/controller/nodelifecycle/metrics.go:98-107) acts as the entry point, called lazily when metrics are first needed. This pattern is consistently applied across all controllers like endpointslicemirroring (pkg/controller/endpointslicemirroring/metrics/metrics.go:137-149), nodeipam (pkg/controller/nodeipam/ipam/cidrset/metrics.go:81-88), and apiserver components (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/metrics.go:98-104).\\n\\n## Prometheus Approach: Dual Pattern with Auto-Registration\\nPrometheus uses both automatic and manual registration patterns. The storage/remote subsystem demonstrates auto-registration via `promauto.NewCounter()` (storage/remote/write.go:38-55), where metrics are created at package initialization and automatically registered. Conversely, the notifier subsystem (notifier/metric.go:33-108) uses manual creation with `prometheus.NewHistogramVec()` and `prometheus.NewCounterVec()`, followed by explicit registration through `r.MustRegister()` where a Registerer is passed to the constructor function `newAlertMetrics()`. The scrape subsystem (scrape/metrics.go:62-120) follows the manual pattern, creating metrics within `newScrapeMetrics(reg prometheus.Registerer)` and registering them via the provided registerer parameter. This flexibility allows Prometheus to support both global auto-registration and custom registries.\\n\\n## Grafana Approach: Global Auto-Registration\\nGrafana exclusively uses the promauto auto-registration pattern with `promauto.NewCounter()`, `promauto.NewHistogram()`, and `promauto.NewGaugeVec()` functions. Metrics are declared at package level in var blocks (pkg/services/notifications/mailer.go:24-34, pkg/infra/httpclient/httpclientprovider/datasource_metrics_middleware.go:16-61). Registration happens automatically upon creation, either at package init time or module load time. This pattern is uniformly applied across all Grafana modules including datasource metrics middleware (pkg/infra/httpclient/httpclientprovider/datasource_metrics_middleware.go:46-61), storage services (pkg/storage/unified/sql/rvmanager/rv_manager.go:27-56), and TSDB instrumentation (pkg/tsdb/loki/instrumentation/instrumentation.go:14-18). No explicit registration calls are needed with Grafana's approach.\\n\\n## Key Differences\\n1. **Registration Pattern**: Kubernetes uses explicit centralized registration through legacyregistry; Prometheus supports both explicit and automatic; Grafana uses automatic only.\\n2. **Registry Scope**: Kubernetes maintains a global legacy registry; Prometheus allows custom registry injection; Grafana relies on the default global registry.\\n3. **Stability Framework**: Kubernetes includes stability levels in metrics (metrics.ALPHA, metrics.STABLE); Prometheus and Grafana do not.\\n4. **Initialization Timing**: Kubernetes uses lazy registration via sync.Once; Prometheus/Grafana register at package load time.\\n\"\n}\n",

Registration occurs through `legacyregistry.MustRegister()` (staging/src/k8s.io/component-base/metrics/legacyregistry/registry.go:37), typically within a `sync.Once` pattern to ensure single registration. The `Register()` function (pkg/controller/nodelifecycle/metrics.go:98-107) acts as the entry point, called lazily when metrics are first needed. This pattern is consistently applied across all controllers like endpointslicemirroring (pkg/controller/endpointslicemirroring/metrics/metrics.go:137-149), nodeipam (pkg/controller/nodeipam/ipam/cidrset/metrics.go:81-88), and apiserver components (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/metrics.go:98-104).\\n\\n## Prometheus Approach: Dual Pattern with Auto-Registration\\nPrometheus uses both automatic and manual registration patterns. The storage/remote subsystem demonstrates auto-registration via `promauto.NewCounter()` (storage/remote/write.go:38-55), where metrics are created at package initialization and automatically registered. Conversely, the notifier subsystem (notifier/metric.go:33-108) uses manual creation with `prometheus.NewHistogramVec()` and `prometheus.NewCounterVec()`, followed by explicit registration through `r.MustRegister()` where a Registerer is passed to the constructor function `newAlertMetrics()`. The scrape subsystem (scrape/metrics.go:62-120) follows the manual pattern, creating metrics within `newScrapeMetrics(reg prometheus.Registerer)` and registering them via the provided registerer parameter. This flexibility allows Prometheus to support both global auto-registration and custom registries.\\n\\n## Grafana Approach: Global Auto-Registration\\nGrafana exclusively uses the promauto auto-registration pattern with `promauto.NewCounter()`, `promauto.NewHistogram()`, and `promauto.NewGaugeVec()` functions. Metrics are declared at package level in var blocks (pkg/services/notifications/mailer.go:24-34, pkg/infra/httpclient/httpclientprovider/datasource_metrics_middleware.go:16-61). Registration happens automatically upon creation, either at package init time or module load time. This pattern is uniformly applied across all Grafana modules including datasource metrics middleware (pkg/infra/httpclient/httpclientprovider/datasource_metrics_middleware.go:46-61), storage services (pkg/storage/unified/sql/rvmanager/rv_manager.go:27-56), and TSDB instrumentation (pkg/tsdb/loki/instrumentation/instrumentation.go:14-18). No explicit registration calls are needed with Grafana's approach.\\n\\n## Key Differences\\n1. **Registration Pattern**: Kubernetes uses explicit centralized registration through legacyregistry; Prometheus supports both explicit and automatic; Grafana uses automatic only.\\n2. **Registry Scope**: Kubernetes maintains a global legacy registry; Prometheus allows custom registry injection; Grafana relies on the default global registry.\\n3. **Stability Framework**: Kubernetes includes stability levels in metrics (metrics.ALPHA, metrics.STABLE); Prometheus and Grafana do not.\\n4. **Initialization Timing**: Kubernetes uses lazy registration via sync.Once; Prometheus/Grafana register at package load time.\\n\"\n}\n",
